  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e7c2fc93-b99e-43dc-a3a5-ef703d38fbc0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18113721028236988767">Things are about to get <i>Wicked</i> in New Orleans.<br/><br/>Twenty-two year old Ivy Morgan isn’t your average college student. She, and others like her, know humans aren’t the only thing trolling the French Quarter for fun… and for food. Her duty to the Order is her life. After all, four years ago, she lost <i>everything</i> at the hands of the creatures she’d sworn to hunt, tearing her world </span>
  <span id="freeText18113721028236988767" style="display:none">Things are about to get <i>Wicked</i> in New Orleans.<br /><br />Twenty-two year old Ivy Morgan isn’t your average college student. She, and others like her, know humans aren’t the only thing trolling the French Quarter for fun… and for food. Her duty to the Order is her life. After all, four years ago, she lost <i>everything</i> at the hands of the creatures she’d sworn to hunt, tearing her world and her heart apart.<br /><br />Ren Owens is the last person Ivy expected to enter her rigidly controlled life. He’s six feet and three inches of temptation and swoon-inducing charm. With forest-green eyes and a smile that’s surely left a stream of broken hearts in its wake, he has an uncanny, almost unnatural ability to make her yearn for everything he has to offer. But letting him in is as dangerous as hunting the cold-blooded killers stalking the streets. Losing the boy she loved once before had nearly destroyed her, but the sparking tension that grows between them becomes impossible for Ivy to deny. Deep down, she wants… she needs more than what her duty demands of her, what her past has shaped for her.<br /><br />But as Ivy grows closer to Ren, she realizes she’s not the only one carrying secrets that could shatter the frail bond between them. There’s something he’s not telling her, and one thing is for certain. She’s no longer sure what is more dangerous to her—the ancient beings threatening to take over the town or the man demanding to lay claim to her heart and her soul.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18113721028236988767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1132164101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132164101" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132164101?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cheesy">cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132164101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer474133175630268675"> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380797199ra/3123382.gif' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>B-But…I usually love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout' title='Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer L. Armentrout</a>’s work! Her characters always feel like they could just jump off the page and stand before you, and her writing always flows perfectly with the story and pacing. Yet, this did not work for me. I had <em>déjà vu</em> sensations at many points into the novel, as if I’ve read this kind of story many times before, NA and its <em>oh-so-imminent</em> aspects aside. It actually felt like the author inspired some of her story’s constituents from <strong>The Hollows</strong>, <strong>Fever</strong> and the <strong>Nig</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText474133175630268675" style="display:none"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380797199ra/3123382.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>B-But…I usually love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a>’s work! Her characters always feel like they could just jump off the page and stand before you, and her writing always flows perfectly with the story and pacing. Yet, this did not work for me. I had <em>déjà vu</em> sensations at many points into the novel, as if I’ve read this kind of story many times before, NA and its <em>oh-so-imminent</em> aspects aside. It actually felt like the author inspired some of her story’s constituents from <strong>The Hollows</strong>, <strong>Fever</strong> and the <strong>Night Huntress</strong> series…but mixed and developed them with a poor and predictable execution.<br><br>Ivy works for the order: she kills fae, those despicable creatures that lure into the human world. She doesn’t have many people she cares about: her parents and her boyfriend both died and she is now left living alone with a certain brownie (similar to a pixie, since they can fly, but uglier, I think) she found on her path, Tink, killing fae after fae, sometimes along her best friend, Val. Except, one day, she finds herself in front of an <em>Ancient</em>, while those were supposed to be held in the Otherworld only. Could it be that a grand danger is to come? When the Ancient escapes (more like the other way around – he is too powerful), she plans on finding him again and, this time, to actually vanquish him. But, she will not be alone on this mission. Ren, her new partner, will be beside her.<br><br>I honestly thought Ivy was a good heroine to read about. She was strong, fierce and snarky by moment and having this nonchalance I admired: <strong>
  <em>‘‘I’d never been shot before. Stabbed? Yes. Thrown around? Most definitely. Almost set on fire? That too. But being shot…wow, this sucked donkey balls.’’</em>
</strong> However, I did think her ‘innocence’ wasn’t convincing. She kept bringing her ex-boyfriend, who died three years ago, up (which got annoying after some time) saying how much she loved him and didn’t feel that close to anyone again since he, Shaun, died…but then she told Ren she didn’t have much experience and that with Shaun they haven’t gotten THAT far. It wasn’t very believable.<br><br>Ren was…a bit strange. Honestly, there are moments when he seemed alpha-like, others when he was acting very childishly and, the rest of the time, he kept popping out cheesy or cliché lines as: <strong>
  <em>‘‘You’re even pretty when you cry,’’ ‘‘I want to hear you scream my name when you come,’’ ‘‘I’ve been waiting all day for you to text or call me’’ </em>
</strong>or <strong>
  <em>‘‘It’s a good thing—a powerful thing to see a female you like wearing your clothes.’’</em>
</strong><br><br>‘Female,’ <em>really</em>?<br><br>The romance overall was okay, but very predictable and containing unsurprising scenes. It could have worked better if, I believe, we knew more about Ren and if this latter would have been more exciting. I thought Ivy’s relationship with Val was overrated. I mean, it was obvious she was the only friend Ivy possessed, but I wasn’t convinced here either that they had the kind of strong bond Ivy seemed to think. The pacing was great, really, but the writing, this time, repetitive and lacking of a throughout style.<br><br>A character I did find original though was Tink, even if he reminded me A LOT of Jenks from <strong>The Hollows</strong> series. He was fun and entertaining! This made me ‘LOL’ so much:<br><br><strong>
  <em>‘‘Let’s talk about sex.’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘No.’’ Rolling my eyes, I walked away.</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Sex is good!’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Shut up, Tink.’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Sex is fun!’’ he continued to shout.</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> I shook my head. ‘‘The only thing you’re having sex with is inanimate objects, so what do you know?’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> He ignored me. ‘‘Sex is best when it’s one on one!’’</em>
</strong><br><br>And so, this was not the best book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> that I’ve read so far. On the contrary, unfortunately. Although, recently, I’ve been having disappointments with my NA reads. Maybe I should keep my distance from them for a while? Nuh-uh, they always have such interesting premises; I cannot resist. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20348781.Loving_Mr__Daniels" title="Loving Mr. Daniels by Brittainy C. Cherry" rel="nofollow noopener">Loving Mr. Daniels</a> is next. *wink* *wink*</span>
  <a data-text-id="474133175630268675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3604674788" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3604674788?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780988982956" href="/book/show/23356038-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3604674788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10840420406653524804"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885537-city-of-bones' rel='nofollow noopener'>city of bones</a> + <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22875400-the-falconer' rel='nofollow noopener'>the falconer</a> = this book<br/><br/>a secret order of special individuals are tasked with hunting down the paranormal (like city of bones), which in this case are evil fae (like the falconer). everything else about this book is classic JLA. entertaining plot, fun side characters, steamy romance, and a cliffhanger you can see coming a mile away. lol. <br/><br/>i cant say this is my favourite book of hers. i am slowly, but surely, making my way through JLAs bibliography (i think this is book #31), and a</span>
  <span id="freeText10840420406653524804" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885537-city-of-bones" rel="nofollow noopener">city of bones</a> + <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22875400-the-falconer" rel="nofollow noopener">the falconer</a> = this book<br /><br />a secret order of special individuals are tasked with hunting down the paranormal (like city of bones), which in this case are evil fae (like the falconer). everything else about this book is classic JLA. entertaining plot, fun side characters, steamy romance, and a cliffhanger you can see coming a mile away. lol. <br /><br />i cant say this is my favourite book of hers. i am slowly, but surely, making my way through JLAs bibliography (i think this is book #31), and although i prefer her more recent fantasy books, i did enjoy this more than some of her others (<i>*cough*</i> the covenant series <i>*cough*</i>). i like that the fae are the villains, as its a uncommon perspective. i think thats was really drew me into the story and its a great set up for the following books.<br /><br />overall, not disappointed with this and will most likely continue with the series. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1068551239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1068551239" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1068551239?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=white-people-kissing">white-people-kissing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=floating-or-falling">floating-or-falling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068551239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7014023000434064998">I'm pretty sure I start off every review for a book that Jla writes by saying something along the lines of this... <b>JLA HAS DONE IT AGAIN!!! Another amazing novel. This lady can write anything. Contemporary, paranormal romance, NA lit, anything. If she published her target shopping list I would read it because I know she would make it amazing.</b> <i>Wicked </i>was so wicked!!! Too me it was like the polar opposite of her <i>Dark Elements </i>series and I loved that (I love The Dark Elements)!I just loved that it </span>
  <span id="freeText7014023000434064998" style="display:none">I'm pretty sure I start off every review for a book that Jla writes by saying something along the lines of this... <b>JLA HAS DONE IT AGAIN!!! Another amazing novel. This lady can write anything. Contemporary, paranormal romance, NA lit, anything. If she published her target shopping list I would read it because I know she would make it amazing.</b> <i>Wicked </i>was so wicked!!! Too me it was like the polar opposite of her <i>Dark Elements </i>series and I loved that (I love The Dark Elements)!I just loved that it was so different.<br><i>Wicked </i>is a paranormal new adult and a first in <i>The Wicked Trilogy</i>. Pretty sure at one point I told Leah I thought I just got pregnant reading this. <b>Whoosh it was so hot! </b>It wasn't just the steamy scenes that made this book. It was everything. The world building, plot, flow, and the characters. Ivy is funny, strong, and awkward. The things that go on in her head are hilarious. Ren is so upfront, charming, and wickedly hot. The relationship between Ren and Ivy is almost insta-love but falls closer to insta-lust. Which I think is a good thing. The things they say to each other (mainly Ren) is so so yummy.<br><br><i>"um, yeah. I do. Baking... is like a hobby." Okay that was a total lie. The only cakes I could bake came out of the box. It was Tink who baked the cakes from scratch. "And why haven't I been offered any cake?"..."You're going to have to get to know me better before you taste my cake."... "Was that an invitation? Because I'm willing to get to know you in any way possible if that means I get to taste your cake." "Invitation for....?" Oh my God. My words replayed. My face turned crimson. "You are such a pervert!" </i><br><br>I really enjoyed Ren as a character so much. He is seriously like the sweet caring version of Roth from TDE. They even both ride motorcycles. He also knows Disney movies. For some odd reason men knowing Disney movies is hot.<b> Hell, Jla seriously can make anything hot.</b> She did some job on Ren. Kid you not this was me 99.9% of the time he was involved...<br><br><div>
  <br>
  
    <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-st-hDB6i4ig/VIud8uaGmwI/AAAAAAAAAss/WDYs3IpnAqU/s1600/775857.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
      <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418436557ra/12785192.gif" height="209" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
    </a>
    <br>
    <div></div>
    <br>
    <div>
      <br>
      He was the perfect leading man. Romantic and Take charge. One of my favorite things however is how Ivy is described. She's a curvy frizzy haired ginger. Loved it! The romantic scenes between the two of them are written perfectly. Saying they were hot would be an understatement. I was reading this at work and had to stop because I couldn't stop blushing. I can't wait to see what happens between these two crazy kids as the story continues. As for sub characters the main ones are Val and Tink. Val is Ivy's best friend and is a little on the slutty side (<i>no judgement</i>). But my favorite, <b>FAVORITE</b> character is Tink. OMG I love him so much!!!! The one foot-troll doll lovin-pop culture junkie-little brownie stole the show. Everything he says is amazing.<i> </i><br><br><i>"Grabbing a scarf off the chair, I threw it at him. He caught it, clutching it to his chest as he flew into the air. "You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!" He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, "Tink is freeeeee!" Ren looked at me. "What the actual fuck?" I sighed. "He's obsessed with Harry Potter. I'm sorry."</i><br><br>The Twilight, Dr. Who, Harry Potter, and Salt and Pepa references he threw around killed me. It had been a long time since I had laughed that hard, and at a sub-character too. He took this story too a whole new level.<i> </i>
    </div>
    <br>
    <i>"He ignored me. "Sex is best when it's one on one!" Stopping in the hall, I turned to where he was doing a pelvic thrust. "Isn't that a George Michael song?" "Maybe. but he was wrong. I like to think sex is best when it's like three on three or something. Seems more adventurous." Whatever. Goodnight, Tink." I closed the door as he broke out in a Salt-n-Pep a song. </i>
  
</div><br><div></div><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-bPCgOmlDAaI/VIua-zDpGMI/AAAAAAAAAsE/rh8puBs3WUA/s1600/wickedupdat.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418436557i/12785193.jpg" height="320" width="299" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>Every character in this book is so perfect. The plot if fast paced and action packed. There was never a dull moment, or a time I was bored. The plot starts strong and doesn't let up. There are two twist in this story. One was very predictable and one I had no clue was coming. I don't think I've ever updated my GR status so many times before, especially out of pure excitement. Seriously wasn't kidding when I said I needed water. This book was like a sauna!! And the ending. Holy sweet Jesus way to leave us hanging!!! <i>Wicked </i>has to be one of my favorite books and start to a series I've read all year.<br><br>Can I please give this more than five stars?!?!?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7014023000434064998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14830990696546503122">I loved the cover but the story was...<br/><br/><span>[image error]</span> <br/><br/>Ivy Morgan is a red headed Fae hunter who lives in New Orleans.   <span id="freeText14830990696546503122" style="display:none">I loved the cover but the story was...<br><br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>Ivy Morgan is a red headed Fae hunter who lives in New Orleans. She is a member of The Order protecting us humans from the lurking Fae. Ivy meets Ren Owens who is new to the area and this chapter of The Order from Colorado. They slowly fall in love all the while they are working together trying to figure out what is going on with Ancients and their plan to use the gateways to enter our world.<br><br>The writing just didn’t measure up to the Lux Series to me and the characters were mediocre. Ren, the love interest was completely bland and the love connection was sadly the same. I just didn’t feel anything for this couple. <br><br>The best character in the story was Tink the Brownie. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492464529ra/22519981.gif" width="390" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The plot twist was predictable and sadly Jennifer Armentrout didn’t bring anything new to the Fae type stories that I have already read. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492464529ra/22519982.gif" width="390" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147691867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12963676533659521686"><b> 4 Tink stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “I'm a lot of things, but today I'm your fucking saving grace.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/wickedjlacollage.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420098160i/13171709.png' alt=' photo wickedjlacollage.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This one was a nice surprise! After seeing a handful of negative reviews on this one, I went into it with lowered expectations. I came out of this reading experience a very happy girl! And after 2 previous books I DNF'd, I need this gem of a story.<br/><br/>First off, this book is very much <b> New Adult </b> genre, so don't go into it thinking it's YA. The fact that in Chapter 1 the MC is discussing getting laid and orgasms is</span>
  <span id="freeText12963676533659521686" style="display:none"><b> 4 Tink stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “I'm a lot of things, but today I'm your fucking saving grace.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/wickedjlacollage.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420098160i/13171709.png" alt=" photo wickedjlacollage.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This one was a nice surprise! After seeing a handful of negative reviews on this one, I went into it with lowered expectations. I came out of this reading experience a very happy girl! And after 2 previous books I DNF'd, I need this gem of a story.<br><br>First off, this book is very much <b> New Adult </b> genre, so don't go into it thinking it's YA. The fact that in Chapter 1 the MC is discussing getting laid and orgasms is the first giant sign.<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/Untitled.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418857558i/12924017._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Untitled.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ivy is a member of an Order that can see fae in our realm. Faeries aren't the good guys, in fact they feed off of humans with deadly consequences. Living in New Orleans, Ivy has a very tragic past and does her best to keep those around her at arms length. That is, until she's assigned a new partner Ren, who is hotness come to life and very much interested in her.<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/Untitled.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418857558i/12924017._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Untitled.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book had me smiling the majority of the time I was reading it. It's not the most original plot, but it was enjoyable and it worked for me. Because my brain is a bit fried at the moment, I'm doing a breakdown review.<br><br><b> What I liked: </b><br>-Ivy: A great mix of kick ass woman with a little but of a vulnerable girl in her, Ivy wants more than the predicted short life span the Order has to offer. Ivy dreams of a future of <b> more </b> and I found that admirable.<br><br>-Tink: Loved this guy, he was freaking hilarious. Especially that Dobby house elf scene. LMAO!<br><br><b> <i> “You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!" He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, "Tink is freeeeee!” </i> </b><br><br>-Ren's determination: While he was spewing a bunch of instalust, Ren made the point that in their line of work, they had to chase after what they wanted with no hesitations. And he wanted Ivy and his pursuit of her was so much fun to read.<br><br>-Pop culture references: I'm fairly certain that this book is self-published, and I feel because of that JLA was able to include references to Harry Potter, The Walking Dead, Amazon Prime etc, which yes will date this book in the future, but gave the book a unique touch that I rather enjoyed.<br><br><b> <i> “Why couldn't he say I reminded him of Ariel or something? Then again, Ariel was kind of stupid, giving up her voice for a dude.” </i> </b><br><br>-Setting: I've always wanted to go to New Orleans, so enough said.<br><br><b> What I didn't like: </b><br>-Pacing: Got a little slow there in the middle and I did have to push myself a bit to keep going. But it soon picked up and remedied itself<br><br>-Cliffhanger: Gah! We have to wait until Summer 2015 for answers!! JLA you wound meh!!!<br><br>-Predictability: &lt;---that pretty much says it all.<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/Untitled.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418857558i/12924017._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Untitled.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Bottom line, if you need a quick, unique New Adult read mixed with a little bit of Urban Fantasy, this book is for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12963676533659521686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3335586273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3335586273" />
    <a title="✰ Liz ✰ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27276528-liz"><img alt="✰ Liz ✰ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451097545p2/27276528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3335586273?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✰ Liz ✰ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✰ Liz ✰ " href="/user/show/27276528-liz">✰ Liz ✰ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=best-leading-lady">best-leading-lady</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3335586273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2964401137704610494"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>“You should've warned me..."</b>
</blockquote><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595427342i/29853427._SX540_.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Wicked</b> is the first book in the A Wicked Trilogy. In the bustling city of New Orleans lives Ivy Morgan a college student who has dedicated her life to the Order. The Order is an organization that works to track and kill creatures. When a dashing young man named Ren Owens comes into town to help the New Orleans Chapter, Ivy is instantly smitten. Ivy is a strong heroine who will do whatever it takes to get the job done. However close Ren and Ivy are becoming, t</span>
  <span id="freeText2964401137704610494" style="display:none"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>“You should've warned me..."</b>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595427342i/29853427._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wicked</b> is the first book in the A Wicked Trilogy. In the bustling city of New Orleans lives Ivy Morgan a college student who has dedicated her life to the Order. The Order is an organization that works to track and kill creatures. When a dashing young man named Ren Owens comes into town to help the New Orleans Chapter, Ivy is instantly smitten. Ivy is a strong heroine who will do whatever it takes to get the job done. However close Ren and Ivy are becoming, they both have secrets that could threaten everything they are building together and take down The Order with one damaging hit! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466701540i/19510149._SX540_.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>“I'm a lot of things, but today I'm your fucking saving grace.”</b>
</blockquote> Told in Ivy’s POV, <b>Wicked</b> has all of the ingredients of a complex paranormal romance with action, passion, and intrigue. The connection between Ivy and Ren is both tender and sweet and it morphs into a burning inferno. <blockquote>
  <b>“I didn't need your permission..."</b>
</blockquote> Overall, <b>Wicked</b> will appeal to paranormal romance fans who enjoy mystical creatures, mystery, and romance. I have long been a fan of Jennifer L. Armentrout and the A Wicked Trilogy is another outstanding series to devour. Be forewarned, you will want to dive into the next book in the series as soon as you finish this one. So have your Kindle ready!<br><br><b><br>🎧This was an audible.com read 🎧<br><br>For more reviews/reveals/giveaways visit:<br><a href="https://craziesrusbookblog.wordpress.com//" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588637625i/29416022.png" width="400" height="185" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450764696i/17467413.jpg" width="" height="50" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://twitter.com/CraziesRus" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450633462i/17450183.png" width="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/craziesrus/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450763751i/17467332.jpg" width="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Crazies-R-Us-Book-Blog-171506803016307/timeline/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450633462i/17450182.png" width="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </a><a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/110273454171852792166/posts" rel="nofollow noopener"></a> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450764696i/17467413.jpg" width="" height="50" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></span>

<div id="review_3361059676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3361059676" />
    <a title="Lisann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann"><img alt="Lisann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592343074p2/104031480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3361059676?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisann" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann">Lisann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780988982949" href="/book/show/24112149-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104031480-lisann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3361059676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260327095799842575"><blockquote>
  <i>“You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!" He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, "Tink is freeeeee!”</i>
</blockquote><br/>Wicked tells the story of <b>Ivy, a 22-year-old student from New Orleans</b>. Since she lost her parents and her boyfriend in an attack four years ago, she lives rather isolated and lets few people come close to her because she is afraid of losing them too. <b>While Ivy goes to university during the day, she spends her evenings hunting Fae that steal the life energy of hu</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7260327095799842575" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!" He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, "Tink is freeeeee!”</i>
</blockquote><br />Wicked tells the story of <b>Ivy, a 22-year-old student from New Orleans</b>. Since she lost her parents and her boyfriend in an attack four years ago, she lives rather isolated and lets few people come close to her because she is afraid of losing them too. <b>While Ivy goes to university during the day, she spends her evenings hunting Fae that steal the life energy of humans to kill them</b>. During one of her nightly patrols she suddenly encounters a Fae that not only <u>has the magic to rob humans of their will but is also able to materialize an object in his hands</u>, in this case a gun. As far as Ivy knew, normal Fae could not do this and in the fight with the mysterious Fae she gets shot by him. With her last strength she drags herself back to the <i>headquarters of the Order</i>. There she meets <b>Ren, another member of the Order who has recently been transferred to New Orleans</b>. Together they try to find out who this Fae was and Ivy soon finds out that there is more behind this than she ever could have imagined. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You wouldn't lie to me, would you, Tink?" <br />"No." He grinned. "You have Amazon Prime.”</i>
</blockquote><br />This book captivated me after the first 100 pages and hasn't let go since. Maybe because the characters of my last book were such a flop, it made me realize how damn well written they are in this story. <b>Ivy is a badass main character who can stand up for herself</b> and as you follow her story her feelings and problems are <i>realistically</i> described so you can easily put yourself in her shoes. <br />Ivys love interest Ren <b>has his heart on his tongue</b> and knows exactly what he wants. Since she has built up a huge wall around herself over the last years, she makes it difficult for him to get through to her on a personal level that has nothing to do with the work in the order. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The fae went down, and before he could retaliate, I went all Van Helsing on his ass.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>I can really recommend this book to everyone who wants to read a great New Adult Urban Fantasy book.</b> The ending is so good, even if it is not completely unpredictable, that you need the second book right away. No seriously, I borrowed it directly from the library and will continue reading <i>now</i>, which is why this review is so short. <br /><u>Nothing more needs to be said, dive into the world of New Orleans yourself!</u></span>
  <a data-text-id="7260327095799842575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1026191180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026191180" />
    <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog"><img alt="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576986930p2/28353412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026191180?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=dont-cry">dont-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed">romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=good-boys-i-love">good-boys-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=sigh-bbf">sigh-bbf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=insta-not-used">insta-not-used</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=hot-hot-hot">hot-hot-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026191180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5904044022291559017"><b>Wicked was seductive, insanely addicting and had moments that were oh so funny. </b> I love picking up a Jennifer Armentrout book there's a great chance that I'm going to love the story.  But somehow I always forget how deeply immersed I become with the storyline and the characters.  So by the time I got to the end of Wicked, I couldn't help shaking my head because I had tears pouring down my face.  Again. <b> I don't know why I'm always shocked that I feel every single tiny moment of joy, hope and utt</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5904044022291559017" style="display:none"><b>Wicked was seductive, insanely addicting and had moments that were oh so funny. </b> I love picking up a Jennifer Armentrout book there's a great chance that I'm going to love the story.  But somehow I always forget how deeply immersed I become with the storyline and the characters.  So by the time I got to the end of Wicked, I couldn't help shaking my head because I had tears pouring down my face.  Again. <b> I don't know why I'm always shocked that I feel every single tiny moment of joy, hope and utter devastation with the characters she creates.</b>  <b>Because that's what always happens.</b>  But her endings, oh my goodness, this one left my heart hurting yet I have lots of faith and can't wait to see where the story will go!<blockquote>
  
    <b>We lived with death and we knew it waited for each and every one of us. We were taught not to fear the inevitable, but again, what we were never taught was how to live on when those around us left.</b>
  
</blockquote>It was so much fun being back in a world that somehow reminded me of the Covenant/Titan series.  I think I'm grasping straws here, but the setting took place in a world much like the one we are living in now.  Plus, the members of the Order have endured a lifetime of training and a dedication that they will protect those around them.  I was fascinated learning everything I could about them.<blockquote>
  
    <b>"Are you hitting on me?" Shocked, I shook my head. "Are you for real?"<br>"My momma probably thinks I'm real."<br>I ignored that. "While I have a stake at your throat?" <br>"You're also sitting on me, and sweetness, if you slide about an inch or so down, things are going to get real awkward."<br>Holy shit.<br>"Or fun," he added, and his lips did that slow curl again, like he savored the whole process of smiling. "I told you I found that move you made to be fucking hot. But I don't think you're going to be down for that."</b>
  
</blockquote><b>Ivy is a member of the Order,</b> and while she spent her days going to college, at night she hunted the fae.  I loved that she had aspirations to become more in life then what she was raised to be.  But it was fun watching her hunt the fae at night.  She was beyond brave and I quickly admired her strength and her perseverance to keeping others safe.  But during the day I got to see many other sides to her.  When she was around Tink, a brownie that she saved and was living with her, the humor that floated between the two of them was electrifying.  And then the naivety and uncertainty that she showed around Ren, a new transfer in the Order, just made me like her that much more.  She was so relatable, real, caring, ahhh you know what?  <b>Ivy was someone that I would value and be grateful to have as a friend.</b><blockquote>
  
    <b>"You're going to have to get to know me better before you taste my cake."<br>Ren opened his mouth then closed it a second before he stopped and stepped right in front of me. I skidded to a stop to avoid slamming into him . The guy behind us cursed and shot us a dirty look as he walked around us. Ren ignored him. "Was that an invitation? Because I'm willing to get to know you in any way possible if that means I get to taste your cake."<br>"Invitation for . . .?" Oh my God. My words replayed. My face turned crimson. "You are such a pervert!" I smacked his chest hard. "That's not what I meant."<br>"That's a damn shame then," he said solemnly.<br>I hit him again, on the arm this time, then stormed around him. "You're such a dog."</b>
  
</blockquote><b>Ren, oh my gosh. *shivers coat my skin* I loved how direct and to the point he was. </b> I loved that he knew right away that he wanted Ivy and he definitely had no problems physically and verbally expressing that to her.  He was forward, seductive, charming and I couldn't get enough of him!  <b>While I'm usually not the biggest fan of a forward approach, he quickly had me begging for more.  The way he treated Ivy, the way he performed his job, actually everything he did I was a huge fan of.  I loved, loved, loved Ren.</b><blockquote>
  
    <b>"You wouldn't lie to me, would you, Tink?"<br>"No." He grinned. "You have Amazon Prime."</b>
  
</blockquote>I couldn't end this review without talking a little bit more about Tink.  <b>Tink was ridiculously hilarious.  That little bastard had me laughing so hard I had tears in my eyes.  </b>My favorite moment with him was the 'Braveheart' scene, oh my gosh I had tears pouring down my face!  Add in the fact that he was obsessed with Amazon Prime and sugar, well I honestly think we could be best friends forever!  And I'm just as excited to see what happens to him in the future books, as I am about Ivy and Ren!  So yes, <b>I easily fell madly in love with this story and the characters and hopefully you will too!</b><br><br>P.S. I love that Ivy reads and that she mentions The Marked Men by Jay Crownover (I love Rule &amp; Asa).<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/2016/07/book-review-end-of-days-penryn-the-end-of-days-3-by-susan-ee/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on Star-Crossed Book Blog</a><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i> <br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1023674207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1023674207" />
    <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog"><img alt="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596881564p2/6603203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1023674207?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog">Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  </a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog?shelf=best-cover">best-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog?shelf=want-to-read-soon">want-to-read-soon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1023674207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14118696306245628442"><b>Chapter One<br/>Sweat dotted my brow. Tendrils of red hair clung to my neck. My legs felt like I’d been sitting in a sauna. I was pretty sure there was a waterfall of sweat coursing between my breasts, and that alone put my mood somewhere between slapping someone and pushing them in front of a trolley.<br/>It was so hot and sticky humid that I was seriously beginning to believe that New Orleans was one of the seven circles of hell and the outdoor seating area of the Palace Café was the gateway. Or the wai</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14118696306245628442" style="display:none"><b>Chapter One<br>Sweat dotted my brow. Tendrils of red hair clung to my neck. My legs felt like I’d been sitting in a sauna. I was pretty sure there was a waterfall of sweat coursing between my breasts, and that alone put my mood somewhere between slapping someone and pushing them in front of a trolley.<br>It was so hot and sticky humid that I was seriously beginning to believe that New Orleans was one of the seven circles of hell and the outdoor seating area of the Palace Café was the gateway. Or the waiting room.<br>A fat drop of sweat slipped from the tip of my nose and smacked off my Philosophy of Human Person text, leaving a little damp circle in the middle of a paragraph I could barely see through the sheen of sweat blinding me.<br>I always thought the title of my class was missing an ‘A’ somewhere in there. It should be Philosophy of A Human Person. But oh no, that wasn’t how Loyola rolled.<br>The small table rattled on its legs as a large iced coffee slammed down directly in front of my book. “For you!”<br>As I peered over the top of my sunglasses, my mouth watered like I was one of Pavlov’s dogs. Valerie Adrieux plopped into the seat across from me, her hand like a claw on top of my iced coffee. A mix of Spanish and African heritage, Val had an absolutely beautiful skin tone, a rich and flawless shade of brown, and she looked awesome in bright oranges and blues and pinks and every freaking color of the rainbow.<br>Like today, Val wore a loose, orange halter that defied gravity, a purple necklace, and as I glanced down, I saw a turquoise peasant skirt. She looked as if she had stepped off a catalog featuring urban chic. If I wore any color other than black, tan, or gray, I looked like an asylum escapee.<br>Sitting up straight, ignoring how the backs of my thighs stuck to the chair, I made grabby fingers at the iced coffee. “Gimmie.”<br>She arched a brow. In the sunlight, Val’s hair had a burnt auburn sheen to it. Pretty. Mine looked like a fire engine. Scary. No matter the level of humidity, her head full of corkscrew curls always looked great. Again, pretty. Between the months of April and November, the curl in my hair got lazy and turned into a frizzy wave. Again, scary as hell.<br>Sometimes I wanted to hate her.<br>“Don’t you have something else to add to that?” she asked.<br>This was one of those times.<br>“Gimmie . . . my precious?” I added.<br>She grinned. “Try again.”<br>“Thank you?” I wiggled my fingers toward the coffee.<br>She shook her head.<br>I dropped my hands in my lap with a tired sigh. “Can you point me in the right direction of what you want to hear? Play a game of hot and cold or something?”<br>“While I love that game most of the time, I’m gonna pass.” Lifting the iced coffee between us, she smiled broadly at me. “The correct response would be, ‘I love you so much for getting me iced coffee that I’d do anything for you.’” She waggled her brows. “Yeah, that sounds about right.”<br>Leaning back in my chair, I laughed as I kicked my legs onto the empty seat to my left, stretching out the muscles. The reason I was probably sweating so much was because I was wearing lace-up boots that ended just below my knees and it was like two-hundred degrees, but I was working tonight, and flip-flops really weren’t conducive to getting the job done or hiding the things necessary to get said job done. “You know I can totally just kick your ass and take the coffee, right?”<br>Val stuck out her lower lip. “That’s not nice, Ivy.”<br>I grinned at her. “It’s true though. I could ninja-kick your ass all up and down Canal Street.”<br>“Maybe, but you would never do such a thing because I’m your best-est friend-est in the world-est,” she said with another wide smile, and she was right. “Okay. What I want isn’t a big deal.” She moved the straw jutting out of the iced tea close to her mouth, and I groaned. “Not at all.”<br>“What do you want?” My second groan was lost in the hum of foot traffic passing the café, and the sound of sirens most likely heading toward the Quarter.<br>Val shrugged one shoulder. “I have a date Saturday night—a hot date. Well, hopefully a hot date, but Daniel has me on the schedule to work the Quarter, so . . .?”<br>“So, let me guess.” I reached behind me, draping my arms over the back of the chair. Not the most comfortable position, but it helped me air out. “You want me to take your shift in the Quarter . . . on a Saturday night? In September. Smack dab in tourist hell?”<br>Her head bobbed an enthusiastic yes. “Please. Pretty please?” She shook the iced coffee, and the chunks of ice rattled in the plastic container enticingly. “Please?”<br>My gaze moved from her hopeful face to the iced coffee and stayed there. “Sure. Why not? Not like I have a hot date.”<br>“Yay!” She shoved the coffee forward, and I snatched it out of the air a half second before she dropped it. A heartbeat later, I was slurping away happily, totally transported to a chilly, caffeinated heaven. “You know,” she began, placing her elbows on the table, “you could have a hot date, if like, you went out on a date once every year or so.”<br>I ignored that comment and continued drinking at brain freeze speed.<br>“You’re really pretty, even with all that hair.” She made a circle with her hand in the general vicinity of my head as if I didn’t know I looked like a Q-tip with my hair piled atop it. “And you have really great boobs and a total tap-that-ass kind of ass. I’d totally do you.”<br>I continued to ignore her as a dull ache started behind my eyes. I so needed to slow down on the coffee, but it was so damn good.<br>“Do you even like boys, Ivy? You know, I swing both ways. I’m more than willing to help a girl out.”<br>I rolled my eyes then immediately winced. Lowering the iced coffee, I pressed my palm to my forehead. “Ow.”<br>Val snorted.<br>“I like boys,” I grumbled as the icepick sensation faded. “And can we not talk about boys or swinging both ways or helping me out? Because this conversation is going to lead to the lack of orgasms in my life and how I need to get naked with some random dude, and I’m not really in the mood to talk about that.”<br>“What do you want to talk about then?”<br>Taking a slower sip of the coffee, I eyed her. “How come you’re not sweating?”<br>Val tipped her chin back and laughed so loudly an older couple strolling by with matching fanny packs stared at her. “Babe, I’m born and raised in Louisiana. My family can be traced back to the original French settlers—”<br>“Blah, blah. Does that somehow mean you have some kind of magical ability that makes you absolutely resistant to the heat while I’m drowning in my own funk?”<br>“Can take the girl out of the north but can’t take the north out of the girl.”<br>I snorted at that. It was true. Having moved to New Orleans only three years ago from northern Virginia, I still hadn’t adapted to the weather. “Do you know what I’d do for a polar vortex right about now?”<br>“Not have sex, that’s for sure.”<br>I flipped her off. Truthfully, I didn’t even know why I didn’t miss a single day when it came to taking my birth control pills. I guessed it was habit from when it actually mattered.<br>She giggled as she leaned against the table, her dark brown eyes surveying my philosophy book. “I just do not get why you’re going to college.”<br>“Why not?”<br>The look on her face suggested the heat had fried a few of my brain cells. “You already have a job—a job that pays extraordinarily well, and you don’t really need to get another one like some of the others do. We don’t have a lot of bennies, and we have probably the shortest lifespan of any job out there that doesn’t involve sky diving without a parachute, but that’s another reason to not waste your time on that crap.”<br>My shrug was my response. To be honest, I wasn’t sure why I started going to Loyola a year ago. Maybe it was boredom. Maybe it was the weird need to do something most twenty-one-year-olds were doing. Or maybe it ran deeper than that, and whatever that was, was the reason behind taking sociology with a psychology minor. I toyed with the idea of being a social worker, because I knew I could do both things if I wanted to. Maybe it had to do with what happened to—<br>I cut those thoughts off. No reason to go there today, or any day. The past was in the past, dead and buried with the entirety of my family.</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407778014ra/10764252.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14118696306245628442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14062456730791354035">I can't say that the ending was shocking or anything, but OH MY that doesn't mean I'm by any means okay with it! <br/><br/>Even though I love Jennifer L. Armentrout and I adore or at least like all of her books , I was quite anxious going into this one. Excited, but anxious. There is always the chance that you won't like a book that much, even, no ESPECIALLY, if you love the author.<br/>Wicked sounded interesting, but not that promising. <br/>So, now I'm even happier to be able to tell you: I absolutely loved this </span>
  <span id="freeText14062456730791354035" style="display:none">I can't say that the ending was shocking or anything, but OH MY that doesn't mean I'm by any means okay with it! <br /><br />Even though I love Jennifer L. Armentrout and I adore or at least like all of her books , I was quite anxious going into this one. Excited, but anxious. There is always the chance that you won't like a book that much, even, no ESPECIALLY, if you love the author.<br />Wicked sounded interesting, but not that promising. <br />So, now I'm even happier to be able to tell you: I absolutely loved this book!<br /><br />For me it was always clear that Jennifer's strength doesn't lie in plot, but characters! I am always able to not only love them as persons but feel WITH them and that is exactly the reason why I love her books! <br />Wicked was definitely no exception.<br /><br />Ivy and Ren were simply amazing. As individuals, but as a couple as well. <br />Like I said before the story in itself is good , but not special at all. That is something you definitely have to keep in mind going into this book. <br />I, however, didn't mind that at all. I was entertained, the writing was easy and hilarous (also Harry Potter and Game of Thrones references y'all), the story had a fast pacing and I just can't wait to read the next installment!<br /><br />Next to the Lux series A Wicked Saga might become my favourite Armentrout series! <br /></span>

    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5616772-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391659353p2/5616772.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1023549016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer173894550683574990">
  Jennifer L. Armentrout never fails to surprise me. 
  
  First aliens, then demigods, followed by gargoyles, and now Fae. IS THERE ANY PARANORMAL CREATURE SHE CAN'T MAKE ME LOVE?!
<br/><br/>Probably not. <br/>
  <br/>Except maybe---owls. I don't think even <i>she</i> could change my mind about owls. And yes, they totally count as paranormal. 
<br/><br/>WICKED is not your average Fae story but it has all the elements I have come to expect and love in a JLA book; strong characters, witty banter, a great story and face fanning roma</span>
  <span id="freeText173894550683574990" style="display:none">
  Jennifer L. Armentrout never fails to surprise me. 
  
  First aliens, then demigods, followed by gargoyles, and now Fae. IS THERE ANY PARANORMAL CREATURE SHE CAN'T MAKE ME LOVE?!
<br><br>Probably not. <br>
  <br>Except maybe---owls. I don't think even <i>she</i> could change my mind about owls. And yes, they totally count as paranormal. 
<br><br>WICKED is not your average Fae story but it has all the elements I have come to expect and love in a JLA book; strong characters, witty banter, a great story and face fanning romance. It's fast paced action had me wishing I too could join the Order (for realz),and the plots twists and turns kept me on my toes right up until the very wickedending where I was like...<br><div>
<br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-c4PCsg0IVUQ/VH4wkrnZC2I/AAAAAAAAG5Y/aZo-z-3fCpI/s1600/awno322182__safe_applejack_animated_image-macro_crystal-empire.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417620618ra/12444308.gif" height="179" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div><br><br>WICKED is a great start to a new New Adult paranormal series and I CAN.NOT.WAIT to see where the story goes next in TORN!<br><br>BTW, Ivy is kick-ass and Ren is totally swoon-worthy, but I call dibs on Tink.<br><div>
<br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-u6KU0LHk30U/VH4u9oAhQ9I/AAAAAAAAG5M/g5eYx74goyo/s1600/trolltrain7907166.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417620618ra/12444309.gif" height="176" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div><br><br></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1023549016">

<div id="review_2396131565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396131565" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396131565?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/25574795-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=a-touch-of-magic">a-touch-of-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=heroine-drove-me-batty">heroine-drove-me-batty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=she-kicks-butt">she-kicks-butt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=did-rolleth-my-eyes">did-rolleth-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=there-will-be-blood">there-will-be-blood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=para-fantasy-series">para-fantasy-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=cliffy">cliffy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=end-of-the-world">end-of-the-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396131565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11869362904277323588"><b>It was OK...ish</b><br/><br/>I think I set my expectations too high. I've had <i>Wicked</i> on my to be read list for yonky donks but never got around to reading it. Saw it on audio, and decided to give it a try. I think the biggest problem was that I would be completely distracted by...stuff, and realise I've missed the last few minutes of whatever the heck had happened. It didn't take me any longer to listen but that was because I decided to not go back and hope for the best. Maybe I should have gone back...<br/><br/>I didn</span>
  <span id="freeText11869362904277323588" style="display:none"><b>It was OK...ish</b><br /><br />I think I set my expectations too high. I've had <i>Wicked</i> on my to be read list for yonky donks but never got around to reading it. Saw it on audio, and decided to give it a try. I think the biggest problem was that I would be completely distracted by...stuff, and realise I've missed the last few minutes of whatever the heck had happened. It didn't take me any longer to listen but that was because I decided to not go back and hope for the best. Maybe I should have gone back...<br /><br />I didn't mind the heroine but I tend to get frustrated with characters who don't move on from the past. Yes, she's had some serious trauma to overcome but, I, myself, am not one to bottle things up inside so I get frustrated when characters do. It's never a good thing to let things fester.<br /><br />Now, our hero, well he comes across as an arrogant, posturing, know-it-all who feels lusty lust for the heroine...and won't give up till she gives in. Sure, I don't mind a determined hero that's been around for awhile, but coming from (practically) a kid, just makes me laugh.<br /><br />The storyline was interesting, although getting hints at the big picture, frustrated me by the end. I never felt like I was on board with the characters. Everyone had secrets and it was hard to keep track of them all and who we are still waiting on to expose theirs.<br /><br />The big DUH...DUH...DUH...moment at the end was more of a - Yeah, yeah, I guessed that ages ago, how could she not have seen this coming? It's a cliffy, but I'm not sure I'm invested enough to want to find out how it will all play out.<br /><br />The narrator does a pretty good job but I don't think I would put her in my favourite's list. I had no problems understanding her and I knew when she was changing characters but her bloke's voice wasn't great.<br /><br />I'm glad I gave this one a go as it had been on my radar for awhile. I may go back...soon...ish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11869362904277323588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1036934840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036934840" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036934840?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780988982956" href="/book/show/23356038-wicked">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">paranormal lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036934840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15586254987941747797">By now I've read JLA a hundred times, I've read most of her books and each and every time she surprises me by how much she still has to give. She writes fun books that you just can't help liking, she is one of the best of her kind. I'm a sucker for paranormalcy.<br/><br/>This one was really wicked. Like really wicked and naughty. I guess maybe because it was new-adult and not young-adult like her previous paranormal works. Nonetheless, I liked it because it was action-packed and the storyline was such tha</span>
  <span id="freeText15586254987941747797" style="display:none">By now I've read JLA a hundred times, I've read most of her books and each and every time she surprises me by how much she still has to give. She writes fun books that you just can't help liking, she is one of the best of her kind. I'm a sucker for paranormalcy.<br /><br />This one was really wicked. Like really wicked and naughty. I guess maybe because it was new-adult and not young-adult like her previous paranormal works. Nonetheless, I liked it because it was action-packed and the storyline was such that appealed to me just by mentioning the word "fae". I had never read a fae book before, I've heard of them, surely, but I had never read a novel centered around the fae. It was interesting for me to get to know what the fae is, I like the beautiful sons of bitches and although they remind me a tad bit of vampires, they still rock.<br /><br />JLA's characters are always interesting, so I'm glad she kept the tradition and created fun, complex, full of enery characters. Ivy is badass, most of the time she can make your head turn completely around by punching you in the face and she is pretty much dreamy and superawesomesaucy. Ren, well, he is kind of an alpha-male so, okay, go Ivy. But he still remains incredibly sweet and mushy. In other words, he's perfect for Ivy. Tink, oh Tink, my little cutie brownie (brownies are something like pixies with wings and six-packs, lol), he is just so adorable and so funny and so little. He was the best add for this book, he was always the one cracking jokes and his sassy mouth is everything the world has to offer.<br /><br />Let's get it on and talk about the ending. Jesus, the ending was intense and it left me what-the-fucking because I thought there was more and I was turning pages to see if there is more material to read. Make haster, JLA, give us the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15586254987941747797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
