<div id="review_1705192859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1705192859" />
    <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth"><img alt="Beth Hudspeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495723320p2/18107143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1705192859?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Hudspeth" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth">Beth Hudspeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=cliffhangers">cliffhangers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1705192859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13212409616930587587"><b>Reviewed by</b>: <a href='https://hellobeautifulbookblog.com/2016/07/26/book-review-wicked-by-jennifer-l-armentrout/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Jennifer L. Armentrout writes a wonderful paranormal romance with twists and turns along the way. With the New Orleans setting and the lively characters this book will have you engaged from start to finish.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Classic JLA. I kind of got hints from The Dark Elements Series and some from The Covenant Series and even some from The Lux Series. With the heroine being a fighter against some sort of evil and a love interest or two. There’s always some type of halfl</span>
  <span id="freeText13212409616930587587" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by</b>: <a href="https://hellobeautifulbookblog.com/2016/07/26/book-review-wicked-by-jennifer-l-armentrout/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Jennifer L. Armentrout writes a wonderful paranormal romance with twists and turns along the way. With the New Orleans setting and the lively characters this book will have you engaged from start to finish.</i>
</b><br /><br />Classic JLA. I kind of got hints from The Dark Elements Series and some from The Covenant Series and even some from The Lux Series. With the heroine being a fighter against some sort of evil and a love interest or two. There’s always some type of halfling. Despite that, Armentrout writes a good paranormal romance. Well, atleast PNR books that I like. Armentrout isn’t a super eloquent writer and I wouldn’t call Armentrout’s writing style “classic” by any means. She always brings her own flare that is unmistakably JLA. I love that about her writing, she is unique to herself and it works for her very well. It says something about an author when you can say something is classic to themselves. She can also crank out books like no other. I have been reading her books for years and still haven’t reached the bottom of the pile.<br /><br />Tink was my favorite in Wicked. How freaking adorable is he? He kinda reminds me of elf with his sugar addiction. When he comes to her rescue with the tiny frying pan and this whole exchange of dialogue below, I think you will understand why you should read JLA books.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Grabbing a scarf off the chair, I threw it at him.<br /><br />He caught it, clutching it to his chest as he flew into the air. “You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!” He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, “Tink is freeeeee!”<br /><br />Ren looked at me. “What the actual f**k?”<br />I sighed. “He’s obsessed with Harry Potter. I’m sorry.”<br /><br />Tink darted back into the room, holding the scarf to his bare chest. “There is no reason to apologize when it comes to Harry Potter.”<br />“You do remember what happened to Dobby, right?” I said.<br /><br />“S**t.” Tink’s eyes widened and he dropped the scarf.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Ivy Morgan is basically a hunter of fae creatures who have come into our world from another realm. She is part of a secret order of humans who have hunted fae as long as they can remember. You are born into it and it’s hard to get out. Ivy likes her life for the most part, but she strives for more by goign to college part time. Even though, she would be hard pressed for an answer as to why she’s attending college. When she meets Ren, the new guy on the block in the order, all of what she believed is about to change.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“When in doubt, get the f**k out.</i>
</blockquote><br />I love New Orleans as the setting for this book. I love anything paranormal with a New Orleans setting. It makes it that much more eerie with the voodoo and weird shit. I’ve never visited New Orleans, but I want to so bad. I don’t live extremely far from there so it wouldn’t be too hard to visit. I would love to see all the history that is there.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“A guy was riding a . . . unicycle on the side of the road, wearing a . . . blue cape. What the hell?<br />Only in New Orleans.”</i>
</blockquote><br />There was a lot more romantic scenes, if you know what I mean, than I thought their would be. But, I mean this is JLA and new adult so I don’t know what I expected. Ren was quite the protector and had some sweet qualities. I felt like he was the typical love interest in her books, but it always works pretty well. I will say there is no love triangle in this one and the drama within the relationship is minimal.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Why couldn’t he say I reminded him of Ariel or something? Then again, Ariel was kind of stupid, giving up her voice for a dude."</i>
</blockquote><br />Armentrout always seems to make me do three things. The first one being laugh. She has really funny dialogue and witty banter. Plus, her characters are always saying something crazy or embarrassing. The second thing being swoon. It might not always be a big swoon, but she writes a great male lead every time. The third thing would be the element of surprise. Like swooning, it might not be huge, but she almost always surprises me with a twist in the plot or a twist from the characters. That combination makes for a great book.<br /><br />That twist at the end, though… She got me.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You wouldn’t lie to me, would you, Tink?” “No.” He grinned. “You have Amazon Prime.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />*******<br />AHHHHH CLIFFHANGERS!!!<br /><br />Going through my list of JLA! ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13212409616930587587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣" href="/user/show/13555222-alex-deranged-kittycat">Alex ☣ Deranged KittyCat ☣</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437718906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6856221181620043184"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417274950ra/12267483.gif' width='500' height='233' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So... I started reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895264.Wicked__A_Wicked_Saga___1_' title='Wicked (A Wicked Saga, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked</a> thinking this would be the book I vote for on goodreads Choice Awards 2015. But nope, not me. This book feels like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/48206.Karen_Marie_Moning' title='Karen Marie Moning' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen Marie Moning</a>'s <i>Fever</i> ugly stepsister. I tried telling myself it's me and not the book. But that's not true. Everything seems forced and underdeveloped in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895264.Wicked__A_Wicked_Saga___1_' title='Wicked (A Wicked Saga, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked</a>.<br/><br/>Ok, what's the book about? Faeries, evil faeries, and <i>the Order</i>, a secret group of people trained to hunt them down and kill them. <s>Merida</s> Ivy is such a warrior. She falls in love with Ren</span>
  <span id="freeText6856221181620043184" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417274950ra/12267483.gif" width="500" height="233" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So... I started reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895264.Wicked__A_Wicked_Saga___1_" title="Wicked (A Wicked Saga, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked</a> thinking this would be the book I vote for on goodreads Choice Awards 2015. But nope, not me. This book feels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/48206.Karen_Marie_Moning" title="Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Marie Moning</a>'s <i>Fever</i> ugly stepsister. I tried telling myself it's me and not the book. But that's not true. Everything seems forced and underdeveloped in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895264.Wicked__A_Wicked_Saga___1_" title="Wicked (A Wicked Saga, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked</a>.<br><br>Ok, what's the book about? Faeries, evil faeries, and <i>the Order</i>, a secret group of people trained to hunt them down and kill them. <s>Merida</s> Ivy is such a warrior. She falls in love with Ren, a member of the secret group Elite <i>
  <b>within</b>
</i> the secret Order. All the while there's a faerie apocalypse coming. <br><br>The nice, interesting thing is that they are both apparently human. No girl-fae impossible love. I didn't think that possible in a book and expected Ren to be some undercover supernatural being, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he's human. It's Ivy who is the dreaded <i>halfling</i> bound to mate with the fae and spawn the end of all men. *sigh* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I also have a problem with Ren using the F word so often and in all forms. And most of the times I feel he's using it at all the wrong moments. It's like the action is making him appear a frustrated teenager instead of a man. Ivy seems also a teenager in spite of her age, what she reads and the shows she likes. Her putting it all on loosing her former boyfriend all those years ago is not so convincing. Had there been a love triangle, too, I would have said this is definitely a <i>young adult</i> book. <br><br>The best characteristic of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22895264.Wicked__A_Wicked_Saga___1_" title="Wicked (A Wicked Saga, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked</a> is <i>
  <b>Tink</b>
</i>! He is to die for!<br><br><b>
  <i>"Let's talk about sex."<br>"No." Rolling my eyes, I walked away.<br>"Sex is good!"<br>"Shut up, Tink."<br>"Sex is fun!" he continued to shout.<br>I shook my head. "The only thing you're having sex with is inanimate objects, so what do you know?"<br>He ignored me. "Sex is best when it's one on one!"</i>
</b><br><br>There are also a lot of references in the book. Some of the best belong to Tink, of course.<br><br><b>
  <i>Grabbing a scarf off the chair, I threw it at him. He caught it, clutching it to his chest as he flew into the air. "You gave Tink a scarf. Tink is free!" He flew out into the hallway like a little cracked-out fairy, screeching, "Tink is freeeeee!"</i>
</b><br><br>There should have been more Tink scenes. He's the reason I'm giving the book 2 stars and not 1.<br><br>All in all, I'm unsure if I'll continue reading the series or not. What I can say is that if you're looking for a good urban fantasy/paranormal book, you should try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112750.Darkfever__Fever___1_" title="Darkfever (Fever, #1) by Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkfever</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1421990.Halfway_to_the_Grave__Night_Huntress___1_" title="Halfway to the Grave (Night Huntress, #1) by Jeaniene Frost" rel="nofollow noopener">Halfway to the Grave</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6856221181620043184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1023746000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1023746000" />
    <a title="Valerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4148118-valerie"><img alt="Valerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364076470p2/4148118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1023746000?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/4148118-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780988982956" href="/book/show/23356038-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=audio-reads">audio-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=jla">jla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4148118-valerie?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1023746000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11297016774421224284">I adore JLA books and the biggest reason is her characters. I adore Aiden from The Covenant series. I came to love Seth as he finished that same series and spun-off to his own, Titans series. Then there's Daemon from the Lux series. He's in a league of his own. But if you take all the things I love about each of these guys and combine them into one guy, you would have Ren from Wicked. <br/><br/><a href='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-b5X8Vui7shI/VITuYMWDLRI/AAAAAAAAWxg/H3LsbSwcZLE/s1600/Wicked-Review-Card.png' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418045614i/12649555.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>He is gorgeous. He is snarky. He is straight forward about his attraction to Ivy. He is so sexy as he's alwa</span>
  <span id="freeText11297016774421224284" style="display:none">I adore JLA books and the biggest reason is her characters. I adore Aiden from The Covenant series. I came to love Seth as he finished that same series and spun-off to his own, Titans series. Then there's Daemon from the Lux series. He's in a league of his own. But if you take all the things I love about each of these guys and combine them into one guy, you would have Ren from Wicked. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-b5X8Vui7shI/VITuYMWDLRI/AAAAAAAAWxg/H3LsbSwcZLE/s1600/Wicked-Review-Card.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418045614i/12649555.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>He is gorgeous. He is snarky. He is straight forward about his attraction to Ivy. He is so sexy as he's always looking for the opportunity to whisper in Ivy's ear and kiss her neck. He's mysterious but he's trustworthy. He's patient with the struggle that Ivy has with a new relationship. He's persistent and just doesn't give up. He turns up in unexpected places and times. He has this incredible vine tat that travels his right arm, over his shoulder and down his back. And the meaning behind that tat had me loving him more. His history has some pain but he's used that to make him better. He lives in the moment and does his job. <br><br>Of course Ren isn't the only character in this book. Ivy is also strong and snarky. I adore her too. The pain in her past has shut down a whole part of her life. She doesn't really know it but it's true. She's determined to be more than just an order member. She does her job but attends college too. Guarded with who she gets to know, she's let in a couple friends but she resists Ren. Good luck with that girl. Did I mention he's persistent? Yeah, he is.<br><br>Some interesting supporting characters make me happy and break my heart. I adore Val and her fun personality. She has an interesting sense of style and says it like it is. I'm so very happy that JLA named her after me. I also loved Merle. She's a character too. JoAnne was a great friend to Ivy. Oh course, Tink is a trip. Love him a bunch. But some lying and choices that I can't understand has at least one of these characters breaking my heart. I want to know what's up and I can't wait for Torn so I can understand. <br><br>JLA's strong characters are always supported by interesting stories. Fae have never really appealed to me. But then JLA had never written about them. I wondered when she decided to write about aliens and then gargoyles but I adore both series. Don't expect to see Fae the way you've seen them before. That's not this author's style. She writes them as she sees them and that's always a unique blend of known lore and twists that can break your heart. I did see one coming in this book but I so wanted to be wrong. The book ends in a whole or many more appropriately under water. I do trust this author to navigate a way out. It's the wait that will be hard on me.<br><br>I love that there's comic relief and some serious sexy times that keeps this story so fun and yummy. <br><br>Of course, I love the writing. I just want to read her books straight through. Nothing gives me pause or has me putting it down. Usually, it's my life that does that.<br>This is a New Adult paranormal read. If you enjoy JLA's other books, then this one is definitely for you. If you love paranormal, then this is a great choice. If you love sexy NA, then you should give this one a shot. I'd recommend this book to anyone over 18 that loves a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11297016774421224284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3202523119741746697"><i>so you know those books that you can't really decide how you feel about them...because they are neither good nor bad? that's this book.</i><br/><br/><b>I, for the most part, love JLA....I did not love this one</b>. I couldn't connect with the characters and it seemed lacking. <u>It got better near the end</u>....the ending makes me actually want to read the sequel when it comes out...but only because I want to see how it turns out...not for any love for the characters.</span>

<div id="review_2209831004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209831004" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7463065-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145167p2/7463065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1515240788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1515240788" />
    <a title="Talia (Red Hot Ink)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink"><img alt="Talia (Red Hot Ink)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472896405p2/25505540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1515240788?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Talia (Red Hot Ink)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Talia (Red Hot Ink)" href="/user/show/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink">Talia (Red Hot Ink)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink?shelf=guys-in-security">guys-in-security</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink?shelf=kick-ass-or-cool-chick-heroine">kick-ass-or-cool-chick-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25505540-talia-red-hot-ink?shelf=warrior">warrior</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1515240788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11546845458285512816">This is more of a 4.5 stars than full 5. Mostly because the first half of the book didn't enthrall me like the rest did.<br/><br/>First things first. This was my second fae book, the first being Dark Fever, which I rated one or two stars if I'm recollecting it correctly. So, yeah, fae are not usually my cup of tea. Armentrout, though, has a way of transforming every topic, creature, and event into read-worthy material. So, here we go.<br/><br/>The worldbuilding didn't really hit me like innovative or over-the-top o</span>
  <span id="freeText11546845458285512816" style="display:none">This is more of a 4.5 stars than full 5. Mostly because the first half of the book didn't enthrall me like the rest did.<br><br>First things first. This was my second fae book, the first being Dark Fever, which I rated one or two stars if I'm recollecting it correctly. So, yeah, fae are not usually my cup of tea. Armentrout, though, has a way of transforming every topic, creature, and event into read-worthy material. So, here we go.<br><br>The worldbuilding didn't really hit me like innovative or over-the-top original. At first, when reading about fae in New Orleans feeding off humans' life force, a deja-vu from the Dark Hunters serie's by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Sherrylin%20Kenyn" title=" Sherrylin Kenyn" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sherrylin Kenyn</a> stroke me. Then it was nothing like it and also nothing like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/669810.Jeaniene_Frost" title="Jeaniene Frost" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jeaniene Frost</a>'s night huntress, even with the red hair possibly giving this rumor a right to be. But not, Ren and Ivy were no Bones and Cat, unfortunately (I've still to find another Cat and Bones for my poor heart to bleed over.)<br><br>Anyway, going back to "Wicked", in true Armentrout fashion, it was a very enjoyable ride, full of humour, a kickass heroine, a wonderful hero with enough Alpha in him to make you swoon, but also a gentlemanly streak to give you the coup the grace.<br><br>I also liked the side characters, how there were various options when it came to who could be betraying them all. I'm not saying it was completely unexpected, but there were enough twists in the story that I was left at least a little blindsided (In a totally good way) in the end.<br><br>At times, especially when it came to Ivy's character and the Orded, this book reminded me of one of Armentrout's first books "Unchained" which to today still doesn't have a sequel (What a shame!!!). However, the fae thing distinguished it from most of urban fantasy. The last 25% of the book had me completely hooked and charmed. Because of... <i>reasons</i>, as Ivy often thinks, but let's face it, these reasons have a name. Ren Owens <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Or should I say Renald Owens. Lol, loved that name. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>image: <span>[image error]</span><br><br>Last, but not least, the dripping hotness. Good Lord, this was hot, in ways that reminded me of her other NA books. There's a certain scene... in a certain club... I'm not gonna spoiler, but just gonna say that that scene put the hot in HOT DAMN. So yeah, folks, just read it.<br><br>Now, if Miss Armentround would release the sequel, that would be great ;)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11546845458285512816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

They could say I looked like the chick from Brave and they were like oh, that's Ivy?<br><br>I needed to dye my hair stat.<br><br>Wait, why was this dude watching Disney movies?</i>'</blockquote><b>I want to let it be known that Wicked made me fall head over heels for a guy who watches Disney movies.</b><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/disney%20reaction" rel="nofollow noopener">

Well guys, he's a stunning specimen of manhood that goes by the name of Ren Owens.<br><br>And if you want to know more about him, you're in luck - 'cause I'm here with the '<b>Top 4 Things Fangirls Need to Know About Ren Owens!</b>'<br><br>#1: <u>He loves the movie Brave (correction: he's in love with Merida)</u><br><blockquote>'<i>'I reached under my pillow, grabbing the iron stake I always kept there. Before he moved, I placed the very pointy end against his throat, right over a very important artery. "Role reversal, b**ch."<br><br>Ren let his arms fall to the mattress as he stared at me through impossibly thick lashes. "That move was really kind of hot." I narrowed my eyes. "You really are Merida." <br><br>"Who in the hell is Merida?" <br><br>One side of his mouth kicked up again. "The chick from the movie Brave with-" <br>"The frizzy red hair. Got it. Thanks. I'm seriously going to stab you."<br>"She didn't have frizzy hair," he argued. "And besides, she was hot." <br><br>I stared down at him. "You think a Disney character is hot?" <br>"Have you seen some of those Disney characters?" <br>"She was not hot." <br><br>(...) His brows lifted. "She could kick ass, therefore she was hot. <br>(...) "This conversation has taken a weird turn."</i>'</blockquote><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/merida%20brave" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2376447086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376447086" />
    <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar"><img alt="Ronak Gajjar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525528784p2/70806774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376447086?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronak Gajjar" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar">Ronak Gajjar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376447086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11357509157011310094">I rather had kick-start when it all started about the war between human world and faerie world. I was like yayyy - <b>Villain Faes</b>! <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525276979i/25471086.jpg' width='450' height='253' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>But then – poof! Nasty plotline did bite me back. *sighs* <br/>Smuty + At time hilarious + <b>Tink</b> + Insta Love + Cheesy + tinge of Supernatural stuff + weak villain aspects! <br/>Concept: <b>3.0/5.0</b><br/>Execution: <b>2.5/5.0</b> <br/>Characters Bespoken: <b>2.25 /5.0</b><br/>World Building: <b>2.25 /5.0</b><br/>Cover: <b>3.25/5.0</b><br/>Writing Style: <b>3.0/5.0</b><br/>Overall: <b>2.25/5.0</b><br/>In short, this photo says the whole damn story of part one: </span>
  <span id="freeText11357509157011310094" style="display:none">I rather had kick-start when it all started about the war between human world and faerie world. I was like yayyy - <b>Villain Faes</b>! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525276979i/25471086.jpg" width="450" height="253" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But then – poof! Nasty plotline did bite me back. *sighs* <br>Smuty + At time hilarious + <b>Tink</b> + Insta Love + Cheesy + tinge of Supernatural stuff + weak villain aspects! <br>Concept: <b>3.0/5.0</b><br>Execution: <b>2.5/5.0</b> <br>Characters Bespoken: <b>2.25 /5.0</b><br>World Building: <b>2.25 /5.0</b><br>Cover: <b>3.25/5.0</b><br>Writing Style: <b>3.0/5.0</b><br>Overall: <b>2.25/5.0</b><br>In short, this photo says the whole damn story of part one: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525276979i/25471087.jpg" width="236" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S.: I loved <b>Tinky Tink</b> :D <br>Romance lovers? This book is been made for you!<br>AND<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525281882ra/25471378.gif" width="555" height="555" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cgmpKTr5RzL5Q1jpUwnUr5nxR0N5tEKUytw6VKEnZCqNCkptlbf2ZHgH2ODWsN6y920zB0s4GXtmetSvmYlktA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rcYVkXzquUBhSi6Q0toZhigKxeNJeivWrN6Xw/2DnkFSxfbV06QIFuAOrplXYxObRpaxp3v2cDkAeHk4xS2e3w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer13616951740004517815">Hey Guys! Please note: I don't send out ARCs for review. If you're interested in reviewing a book of mine before release date, please contact the appropriate publisher. I also do NOT check my Goodreads email.<br/><br/>To email me, please use the below addy. <br/>jenniferlarmentrout@live.com<br/><br/># 1 New York Times and # 1 International Bestselling author Jennifer lives in Charles Town, West Virginia. All the rumors yo</span>
  <span id="freeText13616951740004517815" style="display:none">Hey Guys! Please note: I don't send out ARCs for review. If you're interested in reviewing a book of mine before release date, please contact the appropriate publisher. I also do NOT check my Goodreads email.<br /><br />To email me, please use the below addy. <br />jenniferlarmentrout@live.com<br /><br /># 1 New York Times and # 1 International Bestselling author Jennifer lives in Charles Town, West Virginia. All the rumors you’ve heard about her state aren’t true. When she’s not hard at work writing. she spends her time reading, watching really bad zombie movies, pretending to write, hanging out with her husband and her Jack Russell Loki. In early 2015, Jennifer was diagnosed with retinitis pigmentosa, a group of rare genetic disorders that involve a breakdown and death of cells in the retina, eventually resulting in loss of vision, among other complications. Due to this diagnosis, educating people on the varying degrees of blindness has become of passion of hers, right alongside writing, which she plans to do as long as she can. <br /><br />Her dreams of becoming an author started in algebra class, where she spent most of her time writing short stories….which explains her dismal grades in math. Jennifer writes young adult paranormal, science fiction, fantasy, and contemporary romance. She is published with Tor, HarperCollins Avon and William Morrow, Entangled Teen and Brazen, Disney/Hyperion and Harlequin Teen. Her Wicked Series has been optioned by PassionFlix. Jennifer has won numerous awards, including the 2013 Reviewers Choice Award for Wait for You, the 2015 Editor’s Pick for Fall With Me, and the 2014/2015 Moerser-Jugendbuch- Jury award for Obsidian. Her young adult romantic suspense novel DON’T LOOK BACK was a 2014 nominated Best in Young Adult Fiction by YALSA. Her adult romantic suspense novel TILL DEATH was a Amazon Editor’s Pick and iBook Book of the Month. Her young adult contemporary THE PROBLEM WITH FOREVER is a 2017 RITA Award Winner in Young Adult Fiction. She also writes Adult and New Adult contemporary and paranormal romance under the name J. Lynn. She is published by Entangled Brazen and HarperCollins.<br /><br />She is the owner of ApollyCon and The Origin Event, the successful annual events that features over hundred bestselling authors in Young Adult, New Adult, and Adult Fiction, panels, parties, and more.</span>
